  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_64f9315e-6f3e-4f9c-9f9c-09406e74c210'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText10071797975807553915" style="display:none">DEAD MEN TELL NO TALES...<br /><br /><div>Except to Harry Keogh, Necroscope. And what they tell him is horrifying.<br /><br />In the Balkan mountains of Rumania, a terrible evil is growing. Long buried in hallowed ground, bound by earth and silver, the master vampire schemes and plots. Trapped in unlife, neither dead nor living, Thibor Ferenczy hungers for freedom and revenge.<br /><br />The vampire's human tool is Boris Dragosani, part of a super-secret Soviet spy agency. Dragosani is an avid pupil, eager to plumb the depthless evil of the vampire's mind. Ferenczy teaches Dragosani the awful skills of the necromancer, gives him the ability to rip secrets from the mind and bodies of the dead. <br /><br />Dragosani works not for Ferenczy's freedom but world domination. He will rule the world with knowledge raped from the dead.<br /><br />His only opponent: Harry Koegh, champion of the dead and the living.<br /><br />To protect Harry, the dead will do anything--even rise from their graves!<br /></div></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3058373836?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter" href="/user/show/10477405-peter">Peter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10477405-peter?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3058373836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15904080286411051264">Gosh, what an exciting read. Set in the times of cold war (1976) you see the development of two different characters, Harry Keogh (west) and Boris Dragosani (east) with all the ingredients of a spectacular spy story. Keogh has the talent of speaking with the dead (necroscope) and Dragosani is a necromancer. Who will win at the end? Dragosani often travels to Romania to meet a long buried evil there. It is the real myth behind Dracula (incredibly compelling background story) he encounters. Dragos</span>
  <span id="freeText15904080286411051264" style="display:none">Gosh, what an exciting read. Set in the times of cold war (1976) you see the development of two different characters, Harry Keogh (west) and Boris Dragosani (east) with all the ingredients of a spectacular spy story. Keogh has the talent of speaking with the dead (necroscope) and Dragosani is a necromancer. Who will win at the end? Dragosani often travels to Romania to meet a long buried evil there. It is the real myth behind Dracula (incredibly compelling background story) he encounters. Dragosani changes in the course of events (very eerie description). Will this uncanny man turn into a vampire? At the end there is a nailbiting showdown between Keogh and Dragosani (absolutely loved the Mobius continuum and the Mobius doors mentioned). This is the very first part of a long series and it absolutely got me hooked from the first chapter on. It isn't an easy read, oh no. But if you overcome the first chapter (or the first 10%) you will be richly rewarded with one of the most interesting, innovative and spellbinding vampire stories I ever came across. This book is cult and justifiably so. Highly recommended! It brought back many memories to the 70s and 80s where I grew up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15904080286411051264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1078216306" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1078216306" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33359750-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576550045p2/33359750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1078216306?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/33359750-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15761729-necroscope">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1078216306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11852195265491701034">Brian Lumley is one of my all time favorite authors, and the entire Necroscope series is in my top five of the best books ever written. When I first started reading these books, years ago, I was blown away by the concept of the thing. The best thing of all was a take on vampires that scared the ever loving crap out of me. I thought I had read about scary vampires before, but the Wamphyri were a whole new level of scary. I've read this particular book at least 15 times and at 51 years of age, I c</span>
  <span id="freeText11852195265491701034" style="display:none">Brian Lumley is one of my all time favorite authors, and the entire Necroscope series is in my top five of the best books ever written. When I first started reading these books, years ago, I was blown away by the concept of the thing. The best thing of all was a take on vampires that scared the ever loving crap out of me. I thought I had read about scary vampires before, but the Wamphyri were a whole new level of scary. I've read this particular book at least 15 times and at 51 years of age, I can say that I still get nightmares every time I read it. While I think that the next five books in this series was even more terrifying, this is the one that starts it all and explains what Harry Keogh actually is and all about the E-Branch. If you love the scares, and want the best vampire fiction out there, then look no further. Yep, I'd recommend this book and author. <br />Edit...I'm now turning 56 and I've still not ever read anything so terrifying as these vampires. If y'all want romance, then eff off. You want nightmares? Here is your shit! <br />What terrified Lisa? This has always messed me up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11852195265491701034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2810932120" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2810932120" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2810932120?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780812521375" href="/book/show/1063376.Necroscope">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2810932120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3383566874439534280"><b>”Still holding his victim, now the necromancer crouched down into himself and his jaws opened wide. Needle teeth dripped slime and something moved in his gaping mouth which wasn’t quite a tongue. His nose seemed to flatten to his face and grew ridged, like the convoluted snout of a bat, and one scarlet eye bulged hideously while the other narrowed to a mere slit. Harry stared directly into hell and couldn’t look away.”</b><br/><br/>Harry Keough can talk to the dead. <br/><br/>He discovers something very fascinating: th</span>
  <span id="freeText3383566874439534280" style="display:none"><b>”Still holding his victim, now the necromancer crouched down into himself and his jaws opened wide. Needle teeth dripped slime and something moved in his gaping mouth which wasn’t quite a tongue. His nose seemed to flatten to his face and grew ridged, like the convoluted snout of a bat, and one scarlet eye bulged hideously while the other narrowed to a mere slit. Harry stared directly into hell and couldn’t look away.”</b><br /><br />Harry Keough can talk to the dead. <br /><br />He discovers something very fascinating: though our bodies are no more, our minds continue. The interests that people had while living can be expanded on in the afterlife. If a person is an amateur student of Mesopotamian pottery while living, they will become an expert in the afterlife. <br /><br />So given the fact that I strive to be a renaissance man, an interest in knowing a bit about everything, I would say I will be busy for eternity. The question for all of you is, how busy will you be in the afterlife? I’d say give yourself a good base of interests to work with; after all, eternity goes on and on and on. If you are dull now, you will just get duller. *shudder* That thought is scarier than vampires. <br /><br />Harry can not only talk to the dead, but he can also take advantage of their gifts. Remember in the movie the <i>Matrix</i> when Neo indicating a helicopter asks Trinity, “Can you fly that thing?” She replies, “Not yet.” Then Tank downloads the knowledge of how to fly that specific helicopter into her brain. It is exactly like that. Harry doesn’t ask the dead questions or listen to them lecture. He skips that process and takes into his brain all that they know. This ability is called...Necroscope. <br /><br />His mind can fly out across the world until he finds the dead person who has the knowledge he needs. To harness even more power, he reaches out to August Ferdinand Möbius’s moldering corpse and discovers the secrets of the Möbius Continuum, which allows him to transport himself anywhere he wants to be in multidimensional time. <br /><br />Fortunately, the dead are lonely, so they enjoy their interactions with Harry. <br /><br />The British E- Branch is trying to recruit Harry to help them in a growing ESP war against other countries. The Soviets have their own equivalent of E-Branch, which is also trying to recruit Harry. If Harry doesn’t join the British and he doesn’t join the Soviets, then one or both are going to kill him anyway. He is too dangerous to be left as a free agent to be potentially exploited by someone. <br /><br />Boris Dragosani is a necromancer who can also talk to the dead, but in a much different, more brutal way than Harry’s method. He eviscerates the corpse, plunges his hands into the body, and fondles the organs of the deceased until he knows all that they know. He is the bright and shining star of the Soviet program. He makes frequent visits to Romania to attempt to manipulate a chained, long buried vampire into sharing his secrets without giving him too much of what he wants...namely his blood. <br /><br /><i>”The animal was large and heavy with wool, but even as Dragosani watched so it seemed its bulk shrank down a little, caved in upon itself-diminished! The necromancer sent out a mental probe towards the Thing in the ground, but such was the lusting bestiality it was met with that he at one withdrew it. And still the ewe continued to shrink, shrivel, dwindle away.<br /><br />And as the ewe was devoured, so the cold ground about began to smoke, a stinking mist rising and rapidly thickening, obscuring the rest of the act. It was as if the earth sweated--or as if something down there breathed which had not breathed for a long, long time.”</i><br /><br />Wooly ewes are a fine snack for a vampire (the wool probably cleans away the nasty, centuries old plaque between his teeth), but we know what he really needs. <br /><br />So Brian Lumley sets up this face off between the necroscope and the necromancer as they battle to see who or what will control the fate of humanity. The novel has a Victorian gothic feel, but mixed with much more modern concepts. It is a bit of a slow burn, but then the later third of the novel explodes into a flurry of action. One of my favorite parts is when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Harry raises a long dead Mongol zombie army, and as the skeletons are blown to pieces by modern weapons, the tiny bits of ribs, fingers, and skulls keep attacking. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> *double shudder* <br /><br />The ending will take your breath away. <br /><br />I’ve read a few vampire books, though I wouldn’t call myself a reader of vampire novels. I am always interested in finding the more creative interpretations of the vampire myth though, and this was certainly not like anything else I’ve read before. There are now 18 volumes associated with the Necroscope universe, and Lumley certainly provides a good base in this book to build upon. There is much more to understand about this universe, so at some point I might be tempted to venture forth into yet another segment to learn more. <br /><br />If only I were a necroscope, I could absorb it all in one go from some unfortunate, deceased reader who has read them all, but then what would be the fun in that?<br /><br />If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br />I also have a Facebook blogger page at:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3383566874439534280" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_93747362" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93747362" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93747362?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780812521375" href="/book/show/1063376.Necroscope">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93747362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1076871256388938948"><i>Necroscope</i> deals with the concept of Paranormal Espionage, which could be seen as a forerunner of at least <i>some</i> of the themes prevalent in <b>Urban Fantasy</b> these days. It is, however, presented in a very different fashion. For one thing, this is first and foremost a <b>Horror</b> novel.<br/><br/>The first half of the novel contains a number of historic sequences filling out the back stories of two key characters and laying the groundwork for the second half. One of these characters is the <b>Necroscope</b> of the title, w</span>
  <span id="freeText1076871256388938948" style="display:none"><i>Necroscope</i> deals with the concept of Paranormal Espionage, which could be seen as a forerunner of at least <i>some</i> of the themes prevalent in <b>Urban Fantasy</b> these days. It is, however, presented in a very different fashion. For one thing, this is first and foremost a <b>Horror</b> novel.<br /><br />The first half of the novel contains a number of historic sequences filling out the back stories of two key characters and laying the groundwork for the second half. One of these characters is the <b>Necroscope</b> of the title, who can talk to dead people. The other is a <b>Necromancer</b>, who harvests information from the recently deceased via a form of evisceration (which is <b>every bit as gruesome</b> as you would think). What then about Vampires? Isn’t that what this novel is about? Well, it is, but this novel really sets up the whole Necroscope series, so the Whampyri theme isn’t <i>quite</i> as predominant (yet) as some might have hoped. However, it’s certainly present, and all good things come to those who wait. This book is actually chock and block full of the mystic and the macabre, dealing with everything from "the eye of death" to Vampirism by proxy. There's a <b>LOT</b> of stuff in here.<br /><br />If a phrase like “the Thing in the ground” sends delicious shivers up your spine, you’ll enjoy <i>Necroscope</i>. It has that Eighties thing going, to be sure, just look at the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/229863.Bob_Eggleton" title="Bob Eggleton" rel="nofollow noopener">Bob Eggleton</a> cover (which, by the way, is pretty awesome, in my opinion), but it’s really, <i>really</i> good if you give it a chance. There are some disturbing scenes in here, not all of which concern gore and violence. It’s not <s>a splatterpunk</s> an <b>overly</b> gory novel, which means that a lot of the tension and horror is psychological. <br /><br />The way Lumley approaches the Vampire legend is completely <b>unique</b>, which is saying a lot. The story is really unpredictable too, and I was never <i>quite</i> sure where it was headed, which was great. Just bear in mind that the vampires of these novels aren't sensitive and emotional, they also do <b>not</b> wear designer undies. In the words of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/20561.F__Paul_Wilson" title="F. Paul Wilson" rel="nofollow noopener">F. Paul Wilson</a>: <i>"His Wamphyri are vicious, savage, ruthless, and unrepentantly evil - a feast for the horror fan."</i><br /><br />I suspect that this novel was more influential than most would think. For one thing, there are echoes in here of anything from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14995.Odd_Thomas__Odd_Thomas___1_" title="Odd Thomas (Odd Thomas, #1) by Dean Koontz" rel="nofollow noopener">Odd Thomas</a> to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/359375.Night_Watch__Watch__1_" title="Night Watch (Watch #1) by Sergei Lukyanenko" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Watch</a>. It seems that this kind of thing was alive and well in the Eighties. <i>Necroscope</i> is the first in a trilogy (the sequels being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60836.Necroscope_II_Vamphyri___Necroscope___2_" title="Necroscope II Vamphyri! (Necroscope, #2) by Brian Lumley" rel="nofollow noopener">Vamphyri!</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/636742.Necroscope_III_The_Source__Necroscope___3_" title="Necroscope III The Source (Necroscope, #3) by Brian Lumley" rel="nofollow noopener">Necroscope III: The Source</a>) and has spawned a whole series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1076871256388938948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2355752909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18102703832309311551">I am officially calling it quits on this book. I have been trying to read it for 10 days and barely made it to 35% of a less than 400 page book. No bueno.<br/><br/>I kinda feel guilty about not finishing this, because it was selected for my bookclub, and I hate not finishing bookclub books. BUT, then I remember that life is too fucking short to waste on terrible books, and I have given this one more than enough of my time already. And it's not like I wanted to finish but couldn't... I just couldn't bring </span>
  <span id="freeText18102703832309311551" style="display:none">I am officially calling it quits on this book. I have been trying to read it for 10 days and barely made it to 35% of a less than 400 page book. No bueno.<br><br>I kinda feel guilty about not finishing this, because it was selected for my bookclub, and I hate not finishing bookclub books. BUT, then I remember that life is too fucking short to waste on terrible books, and I have given this one more than enough of my time already. And it's not like I wanted to finish but couldn't... I just couldn't bring myself to want to keep reading. <br><br>The writing in this book is... not good. It is a product of the melodramatic 80's, and wears that badge proudly on the pocket-protector of its button down plaid shirt... under the sleeveless denim jacket with all the Misfits patches and studs and spikes on it. Probably. There are exclamation points in exposition, which I HATE. It's so juvenile and every time I see it, I immediately start disliking the book. If it is not INTENTIONALLY written for kids, there shouldn't be exclamatory exposition. Save it for over-dramatic dialogue, not your narrative. <br><br>This is slooooow to start, which is somewhat crazy to say since the book actually starts with one of the main characters eviscerating a corpse and learning secret information about an assassination plot from the dead man's flesh, and then immediately helping to thwart said assassination attempt. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526618659ra/25560206.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then 100 pages of boring, followed by about 20 pages of Bond villain level melodramatic Evil with a capital E. <br><br>The boring was a whole lot of junk about the main character, who at this point, was only 13, being bullied at school for being different, a dreamer... and then suddenly, after sitting on the headstone of a math genius, becoming exceptional at math. Like 100 pages of school stuff, including teacher conferences about the kid, and WTF-I-THOUGHT-THIS-WAS-A-VAMPIRE-NOVEL, math homework problems. Plural. Seriously. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526619880i/25560227._SY540_.jpg" height="450" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526619880i/25560228._SY540_.jpg" height="450" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526619880i/25560229._SY540_.jpg" height="450" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ugh. ALL of that, just to hammer the point home to the reader that Harry is now a supernatural/paranormal math whiz... by beating around the bush. I know this is a thing, getting the reader to understand what's going on without coming out and saying it directly, but it was not skillfully used in this book. I would like those hours of my life back, please.<br><br>(PS, sorry for the awkward pics and fat fingers... I was trying to snap these pics from my cell while waiting for a doctor's appointment.)<br><br>Anywho, so that's the boring... but then there's the melodramatic Evil! Dun dun dunnnnnnnnn! Here comes another fat-finger pic, because I just don't care enough to transcribe this awful catastrophe of writing and will cheat and post the image that I snapped of it instead of quoting it. Read on... if you're morbidly curious, or just have a strong desire to see what it feels like for your eyeballs to try to roll themselves right out of your skull. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526620636i/25560256._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's just one page. It didn't take long after that point for me to realize that I couldn't, nay, WOULDN'T make it through 65% more of that. And this is a series. There are MORE WHOLE BOOKS, presumably just like this. WHY??<br><br>Well, to be fair, I didn't get to the "cool" stuff, the battle vs good and evil (sorry Evil) stuff. Harry has switched schools, and we're learning about why Dragosaaaannniiii goes home to Romania every chance he gets. (Spoiler: He's being groomed by Evil Vampire Daddy to be Evil, so that he can release EVD from his imprisonment and thus TAKE OVER THE WORLD!!!) So I was still in the story set-up phase... but I just no longer cared. Kill everyone, Evil Vampire guy. Cool. You'll put me out of my misery. <br><br>I will say that there were cool drawings in the book... but that's about the only positive I have to say about this. Here are a few examples: <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526621143i/25560266._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526622323i/25560308._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526621143i/25560267._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah, so I've returned this back to the library, and I am officially moving on. I'll try not to rant TOO much at my bookclub. Maybe. =\</span>
  <a data-text-id="18102703832309311551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_115418649" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115418649" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3878356-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115418649?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/3878356-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780812521375" href="/book/show/1063376.Necroscope">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115418649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9751661783024076731">A common criticism of Cold-War era spy novels is that they do not have enough vampires. Brian Lumley addresses that problem in Necroscope, where Harry Keogh saves the world from monsters and Communism. <br/><br/>For those of you who don't know Latin, a Necroscope is someone who can scope the dead, which means Harry can have pleasant chats with the deceased to learn their secrets and even absorb their powers for his own. This ability comes in handy when Harry is enlisted by British Intelligence's ESP branc</span>
  <span id="freeText9751661783024076731" style="display:none">A common criticism of Cold-War era spy novels is that they do not have enough vampires. Brian Lumley addresses that problem in Necroscope, where Harry Keogh saves the world from monsters and Communism. <br /><br />For those of you who don't know Latin, a Necroscope is someone who can scope the dead, which means Harry can have pleasant chats with the deceased to learn their secrets and even absorb their powers for his own. This ability comes in handy when Harry is enlisted by British Intelligence's ESP branch to fight a KGB vampire named Boris Dragosani. <br /><br />This plot sounds ridiculous and you're probably wondering if Brian Lumley is a slightly retarded twelve year old, but this book is awesome, largely because the writing is so good. Lumley's prose reminds me of a Savile Row suit. It's crisp, understated, and distinctly British. It has an authority that makes the lunatic plot sound almost plausible. <br /><br />The book also has one of the greatest cover illustrations I have ever seen. Do you see that freaking vampire skull with a tongue coming out of it that looks like it wants to violate you? How creepy is that?<br /><br />I feel like I'm not selling this book enough, so I'll just finish by saying that any fan of Dick Francis will like this book. It's British and fun and is more intellectually satisfying than a book with a vampire skull on the cover should be. It's a great read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9751661783024076731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3592256987" />
    <a title="Gary " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27528763-gary"><img alt="Gary " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499717454p2/27528763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3592256987?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary " href="/user/show/27528763-gary">Gary </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27528763-gary?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3592256987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17713681962150959020">I am glad I discovered this author.This book read a little like a Dario Argento 80s film mixed with early Robert Mcammon (which is a good thing to me). The plot was excellent and the ideas are big. This book bordered a bit on sci-fi even. It mixed together concepts of the afterlife with science, and legends. It's hard to review the book without including spoilers.<br/>Like any good story true to the 80s vibe, it has over the top action that seems go on for even longer than it does, and usually I am n</span>
  <span id="freeText17713681962150959020" style="display:none">I am glad I discovered this author.This book read a little like a Dario Argento 80s film mixed with early Robert Mcammon (which is a good thing to me). The plot was excellent and the ideas are big. This book bordered a bit on sci-fi even. It mixed together concepts of the afterlife with science, and legends. It's hard to review the book without including spoilers.<br />Like any good story true to the 80s vibe, it has over the top action that seems go on for even longer than it does, and usually I am not a fan of that, but it works in this case. The build up is so solid, and the ideas so big, that they swallow any of the impurities in the plot and simply drive it forward. <br />I completely understand why Lumley isn't for everyone. It takes a certain scifi/horror suspension of disbelief to remain even when verisimilitude hangs by the neck. I really needed a read like this in mid -October in the midst of a pandemic. It took my mind away from daily madness into created madness which is always more fun. Oh, and Harry is awesome.<br />4.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17713681962150959020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_90241335" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90241335" />
    <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon"><img alt="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572581488p2/1209800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90241335?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="colleen the convivial curmudgeon" href="/user/show/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon">colleen the convivial curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780812521375" href="/book/show/1063376.Necroscope">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1209800-colleen-the-convivial-curmudgeon?shelf=horror-esque">horror-esque</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90241335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8132746933155875656">2.5<br/><br/>I'm really undecided about this book. It wasn't bad, but it didn't grip me... <br/><br/>Where to start? <br/><br/>It was a bit slow off the bat. I was reading about the Russian ESPers and sort of wondering where everything was going, and when the actual story was going to get set-up. Looking back I suppose it was getting set up at the time, but it didn't feel like it.<br/><br/>Then we got to Harry, and I was much more interested. For awhile, I dreaded the parts where we went back to Dragosani. Ok, not dreaded, but I certa</span>
  <span id="freeText8132746933155875656" style="display:none">2.5<br /><br />I'm really undecided about this book. It wasn't bad, but it didn't grip me... <br /><br />Where to start? <br /><br />It was a bit slow off the bat. I was reading about the Russian ESPers and sort of wondering where everything was going, and when the actual story was going to get set-up. Looking back I suppose it was getting set up at the time, but it didn't feel like it.<br /><br />Then we got to Harry, and I was much more interested. For awhile, I dreaded the parts where we went back to Dragosani. Ok, not dreaded, but I certainly didn't like them as much as the parts with young Harry. And then it sort of reversed, and Dragosani's story became more interesting, and Harry, after skipping a few years, sort of became stunted. There wasn't really any more development in the character.<br /><br />I think that's the thing. This book spent a lot of time on what I consider backstory and set-up. And that would be fine, except the characters were sort of thin. I mean, I don't mind things being a bit slow or thin plotwise if we're getting some juicy character stuff, but after the initial set-up and self-discovery of the two's individual powers, it just seemed rather repetitive.<br /><br />I kept waiting for something to happen... but when things finally happened, it all seemed so, well, predictable, I suppose. It unfolded as we knew it must. The action bit at the end was denoument, the real climax happening when Harry fully realized his powers. But it was just so sudden. I mean, after belaboring the earlier years and development, it all sort of clicked too neatly.<br /><br />I also was expecting to be, well, horrified, I suppose. I was grossed out a few times at some of the descriptions. (Not to mention conflicted about the whole 'I really did the things they credited to Vlad, because I like Vlad, damnit.) But I was never held in suspense. My heart didn't race, my palms didn't sweat... I was never really caught up in the story enough to get truly involved, and I never really felt any impending terror.<br /><br />Meh.<br /><br />I bumped it up a few notches, though, because I did like the very end... the resolution and the revenge. And I was glad that the epilogue explained something I didn't understand from earlier in the story. And I was glad that everything was tied up in this story. It left you with enough of a hook to continue to series, but also wrapped things up nicely if you're not that interested in continuing. And, frankly, I'm undecided. (For a minute or two I was terrified it was going to end in a cliffhanger, so I was extra-relieved with the ending.)<br /><br />In fairness, horror isn't really my forte, and, perhaps, my expectations were a bit too high since this book came so highly recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8132746933155875656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81508349" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81508349" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81508349?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780812521375" href="/book/show/1063376.Necroscope">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=horror">horror</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=magic-powers">magic-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=necromancy">necromancy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=needs-cover-upl">needs-cover-upl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=wordy">wordy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81508349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1779576565813338095"><br/>It seems like I’ve had Necroscope and some of its sequels on my bookshelves forever. I think my early twenties I tried reading one of them and got bored in the first chapter so didn’t get back to it. Thanks for a group read at Horror Aficionados group, I finally dug in, stuck with it, and soon became absorbed.<br/><br/>It still takes a mighty long time to take off, but it’s just a slower style, a long tome that promises interest but divides its action sequences randomly. When fight is present, it stands o</span>
  <span id="freeText1779576565813338095" style="display:none"><br />It seems like I’ve had Necroscope and some of its sequels on my bookshelves forever. I think my early twenties I tried reading one of them and got bored in the first chapter so didn’t get back to it. Thanks for a group read at Horror Aficionados group, I finally dug in, stuck with it, and soon became absorbed.<br /><br />It still takes a mighty long time to take off, but it’s just a slower style, a long tome that promises interest but divides its action sequences randomly. When fight is present, it stands out and doesn’t hold back punches. <br /><br />Harry is an outcast child trying to fit in at school, blessed with the powers of speaking to the dead. Some may call that a curse, but for him it works as he keeps the dead company. There’s an especially sad death where he shows later he can learn their skills by allowing them temporary possession and getting out of tough spots. When Harry was on the page, I was riveted to the story, loving to read through his viewpoints and what he went through.<br /><br />The villains of the story were just as fascinating, if not more so. Dragosani is a demented power-seeker who has uncovered a vampire buried deep in the ground. He himself has learned how to unlock the secrets of the dead, but instead of the subtle dance and conversation Harry uses, he rapes it from their minds when they’ve first fallen and are still fresh. Telepathically the evil vampire Ferenczy communicates with him, bringing him closer with knowledge as the web.<br /><br />It’s a serious book with little joy, but the evil Ferenczy managed to amuse me, especially when teasing Dragosani about his lack of experience. I can’t help but like the putrid character – he’s diseased in soul and mean as a snake, but he’s entertaining to read about.<br /><br />Unfortunately the book finds itself spending a ridiculous amount of time in the heads of other characters too – characters in political positions that I care absolutely nothing about. The political angles and subplots mixed with these dry characters made the book duller than it deserved to be.<br /><br />Overall my rating is strong (4 stars), and I was riveted, but I had to skim sometimes through some dull parts. Politics bore me like nothing else does.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1779576565813338095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_27587265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27587265" />
    <a title="Lanica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1336787-lanica"><img alt="Lanica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217471726p2/1336787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27587265?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lanica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lanica" href="/user/show/1336787-lanica">Lanica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780812521375" href="/book/show/1063376.Necroscope">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Traditional Horror fans, Lovecraft fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=lanica-s-library">lanica-s-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=series-complete">series-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27587265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5851570950885400386">My husband has been on a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9494.H_P__Lovecraft' title='H.P. Lovecraft' rel='nofollow noopener'>H.P. Lovecraft</a> kick lately. He's reading everything, including stories by authors who have been influenced by 'The Master'. He reads the intro's to me for some of these short stories, especially when he sees something by an author he knows I've read. Such was the case with Brian Lumley. I have copies of my Necroscope books on my shelves, I read them when they first came out and enjoyed them so much I've kept intending to re-read them. (Yes, I was a middle and high school</span>
  <span id="freeText5851570950885400386" style="display:none">My husband has been on a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9494.H_P__Lovecraft" title="H.P. Lovecraft" rel="nofollow noopener">H.P. Lovecraft</a> kick lately. He's reading everything, including stories by authors who have been influenced by 'The Master'. He reads the intro's to me for some of these short stories, especially when he sees something by an author he knows I've read. Such was the case with Brian Lumley. I have copies of my Necroscope books on my shelves, I read them when they first came out and enjoyed them so much I've kept intending to re-read them. (Yes, I was a middle and high school girl reading horror novels about vampires in the 80's.) So, one day Brad asks me, "Have you ever read Brian Lumley?" and I'm drawn irresistibly back to the series.<br /><br />First off, they are dated. The Russians vs. the US and England. The Russians are EVIL, the Americans are...well, not quite saints...but the good guys nonetheless. Perhaps a first read would be best thought of as Historical Fiction and it would be easier to overlook the lack of technology and odd politics. <br /><br />Second, writing styles have changed over time. We, today, are used to fast-paced. Everything is faster today than it was when Necroscope was written. So, go into it expecting it to read a little slow in the beginning. It's still damn fine writing!<br /><br />Third, a great character lives on. I still love Harry Keogh today as much as I did in the 80's and 90's.<br /><br />Fourth, a great plot is timeless. Good vs Evil. Vampires who are truly evil, horrible creatures. Secret societies that remain secret throughout the books. And, I love the way the dead are handled in this book. It's fascinating to think about the great masters and what they would do with infinite time.<br /><br />So, I guess it's obvious that I love this book and would recommend it to anyone who likes Horror. Notice, I didn't say vampires. Today's 'vampire' lovers would probably not like this traditional depiction of the monsters. But, hey...all that shimmers is not gold.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5851570950885400386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_330779977" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5846407-bill?shelf=2016-ha-reading-challenge">2016-ha-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer330779977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15235306710959456745">There’s a lot going on in this one. It is much more than the standard blood sucker tale that I thought it was going to be. Brian Lumley pens a unique take on the vampire mythos and adds some very cool paranormal esponiage elements as well. His characterizations were very well drawn and while the pacing is slow at times, it never disengaged me from the storyline. It had a real “old school horror” feeling throughout. Excellent. 4+ Stars.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_192132523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780812521375" href="/book/show/1063376.Necroscope">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5919799-kenneth-mckinley?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5919799-kenneth-mckinley?shelf=own-kindle">own-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5919799-kenneth-mckinley?shelf=own-paperback">own-paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192132523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16602592755888445178">A story with a character that can talk to the dead, one that can extract the dead's secrets, one that can give the "evil eye", a vampire, zombies, British and Russian secret agencies that employ agents with all sorts of ESP talents, and a sci-fi space/time continuum all set in the middle of the Cold War. How can Lumley pack so much goodness in 500 pages? <br/><br/>Necroscope is the book that started a horror series franchise before horror series were considered the norm. Lumley crafts a tale that was revo</span>
  <span id="freeText16602592755888445178" style="display:none">A story with a character that can talk to the dead, one that can extract the dead's secrets, one that can give the "evil eye", a vampire, zombies, British and Russian secret agencies that employ agents with all sorts of ESP talents, and a sci-fi space/time continuum all set in the middle of the Cold War. How can Lumley pack so much goodness in 500 pages? <br /><br />Necroscope is the book that started a horror series franchise before horror series were considered the norm. Lumley crafts a tale that was revolutionary for its time. Shades of Lovecraft permeate through the story as we get to know the protagonist, Harry Keough and antagonist, Boris Dragosani. Harry is a teenager in Great Britain who is learning to use his newfound ability, talking to the dead, and we get to watch the young necroscope learn and grow through the first two-thirds of the book. At the same time, we're introduced to Dragosani, a Romainian who works for the secret Soviet ESP agency. Boris is a necromancer and has the ability to extract secrets from the dead through gruesome mutilations. He also returns to his homeland in Wallachia every year to talk to the mysterious corpse buried in the mountains that gave him his unique ability. The story unfolds as we watch the two learn to harness their abilities and leads towards their eventual showdown.<br /><br /> The setting is the 1970s and it's in the middle of the Cold War and for anyone that grew up during this time, it adds an extra dose of suspicious unease throughout the story. Lumley does a wonderful job setting up the characters in a way that demands you to keep turning the pages. There are so many interesting ideas explored in Necroscope that only scratch the surface. I only hope that the rest of the books in the series delves into each and every one of them much, much further.<br /><br />4 out of 5 stars<br /><br /><br />You can also follow my reviews at the following links:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://kenmckinley.wordpress.com">https://kenmckinley.wordpress.com</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5919799-ken-mckinley">https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5...</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/profile/A2J1JOKW56F2YT">http://www.amazon.com/gp/profile/A2J1...</a><br /><br />TWITTER - @KenMcKinley5</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7664302979712980067">Really more like 4.5 stars, but I'll be generous because there were entire sections here that were 5-star worthy. The first 1.5 hours or so of the audio recording were a bit long-winded and made me worry that I'd been duped into reading a book solely about political espionage (or in this case, E.S.P.ionage). However, once that bit was over the story really unfolded and took off in a couple of different and more interesting directions. I really enjoyed listening to the sections focusing on Harry </span>
  <span id="freeText7664302979712980067" style="display:none">Really more like 4.5 stars, but I'll be generous because there were entire sections here that were 5-star worthy. The first 1.5 hours or so of the audio recording were a bit long-winded and made me worry that I'd been duped into reading a book solely about political espionage (or in this case, E.S.P.ionage). However, once that bit was over the story really unfolded and took off in a couple of different and more interesting directions. I really enjoyed listening to the sections focusing on Harry Keogh and his special talent (no spoilers here) and Boris Dragosani's "dance" with the devilish vampire Ferenczy. As for the level of gross and gory, the most graphic scene took place within the first hour or so, just to give the reader the picture of Dragosani's unique "gift." The novel was very intelligently written; it wasn't just a gore-fest with no substance. After the first 1.5 hours where the story was being set up and I was trying to keep track of the characters, I was never bored. (I tend to avoid very long audio books unless very highly recommended.) I understand that Necroscope is the first in an extensive series of books. I've already got my hands on the second and third installments--which it appears are not yet available in audio format. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9436495369336014753">First few chapters are slow. Very slow. But then the book picks up and just keeps getting better. What I'd believed to be a vampire/horror novel revealed itself to be much more. Necroscope is a Cold War spy novel, where world powers use ESP-gifted agents to spy, interrogate, and assassinate. There is a vampire. It's a beautifully grotesque re-imagining of the monster, more Lovecraft than Stoker. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3131123723" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3131123723" />
    <a title="Matt (TeamRedmon)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3464026-matt-teamredmon"><img alt="Matt (TeamRedmon)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562023660p2/3464026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3131123723?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt (TeamRedmon)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt (TeamRedmon)" href="/user/show/3464026-matt-teamredmon">Matt (TeamRedmon)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3131123723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10623548532676359728">I ended up liking this one but there were times at the beginning that I wanted to DNF. The story starts off extremely slowly with lots of character development on the two main characters Boris Dragosani and Harry Keogh. As a math teacher, I enjoyed the multiple chapters dedicated to Harry's performance in math class at school but if I wasn't a math nerd, I'd have given up then. But once the story got going...eventually, I really enjoyed myself. There are references to Bram Stoker's Dracula and t</span>
  <span id="freeText10623548532676359728" style="display:none">I ended up liking this one but there were times at the beginning that I wanted to DNF. The story starts off extremely slowly with lots of character development on the two main characters Boris Dragosani and Harry Keogh. As a math teacher, I enjoyed the multiple chapters dedicated to Harry's performance in math class at school but if I wasn't a math nerd, I'd have given up then. But once the story got going...eventually, I really enjoyed myself. There are references to Bram Stoker's Dracula and the characters know about the vampire myth which led to some interesting exchanges when the vampire actually shows up. <br /><br />The characters of Dragosani and Keogh are two sides of the same coin, Keogh is a Necroscope (can hear the thoughts of the dead) and Dragosani is a Necromancer (can get information from the dead by fondling their internal organs). Necroscope is primarily their story. While Lumley does a wonderful and original job handling the myth of the vampire, this book is mostly about those two men and their journey towards inevitable confrontation with each other. The journey to that ultimate battle is brutal, interesting, and quite weird and Harry Keogh is one of my new favorite characters. I'm quite excited to discover a new, and quite extensive, series that revolve around the Necroscope. I'll definitely be reading those eventually.<br /><br />I enjoyed this quite a bit and recommend it to anyone that is looking for an original take on vampires. Just be sure to stick with it through the first 100-150 pages, it's worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10623548532676359728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1338127415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1338127415" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1338127415?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1338127415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14644038271647954429">Incredibly eerie and strange, <i>Necroscope</i> was a fairly interesting horror novel.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1338127415">

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_1338127415'><a id="like_count_review_1338127415" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1338127415?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">9 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F66655.Necroscope">Like</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1615604680" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1615604680" />
    <a title="F.R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1309606-f-r"><img alt="F.R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544886612p2/1309606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1615604680?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="F.R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="F.R." href="/user/show/1309606-f-r">F.R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1615604680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8685637872335055980">Whenever I’ve come across a Brian Lumley short story, in one of Stephen Jones’s annual compilations or elsewhere, I’ve been hugely impressed. It’s fair to say that Lumley writes Lovecraftian better than Lovecraft does, as he gets to the eldritch horror of it whilst actually being able to write decent, readable prose. As such for the last ten or fifteen years I’ve been meaning to read ‘Necroscope’, his most famous novel and the one I always used to see in Smiths when I was kid. Now ten or fifteen</span>
  <span id="freeText8685637872335055980" style="display:none">Whenever I’ve come across a Brian Lumley short story, in one of Stephen Jones’s annual compilations or elsewhere, I’ve been hugely impressed. It’s fair to say that Lumley writes Lovecraftian better than Lovecraft does, as he gets to the eldritch horror of it whilst actually being able to write decent, readable prose. As such for the last ten or fifteen years I’ve been meaning to read ‘Necroscope’, his most famous novel and the one I always used to see in Smiths when I was kid. Now ten or fifteen years may seem like a ridiculous amount of time to want to read something and not actually get around to reading it and absolutely I agree with you. What can I say? I’m just incompetent and easily distracted.<br /><br />The biggest surprise for me on picking up ‘Necroscope’ is how un-Lovecraftian it actually is. Yes, there are faint traces of Lovecraft, but there are always faint traces of Lovecraft in every modern horror. Even if the writer hasn’t themselves read H.P. Lovecraft they will certainly have read writers that have, and so the whole thing gets passed on by osmosis. But no, the biggest influence here is – of all people – John Le Carré. This is the taut, charged and exciting cold war horror novel, with espionage games fought by those with paranormal abilities.<br /><br />What on earth have I been doing over the last ten/fifteen years? I feel like I’ve missed out.<br /><br />In the north of England, Harry Keogh is growing up, a strange and withdraw young boy who spends a lot of time hanging around graveyards and who seems to have knowledge beyond his years. He is the necroscope of the title, a young man who is able to communicate with the dead. In Russia though there is a man with similar abilities - Boris Dragosani – only he is a necromancer and his ways of communing with the dead are a lot less pleasant than Keogh’s. Both countries have ultra-secret government departments designed to fight the enemy through supernatural means, so it’s not long before both are known to their respective agencies and on a course to confront each other.<br /><br />It’s not hard to imagine this been scribbled down by Lumley’s right hand, while a well-thumbed edition of ‘Tinker, Tailor, Soldier, Spy’ rested by his left, but first and foremost this is a horror novel. Believe me, if you don’t have a strong stomach then this is not for you. The opening chapter finds Boris Dragosani demonstrating his skills below a chateau near Moscow and it is one of the most impressively gory things I’ve read in a long while. That’s not to say the whole book is written in that blood stained vein, Lumley knows that a little bit of gore goes a long way, but he also knows that the audience for a book called ‘Necroscope’ doesn’t want him to skimp on it.<br /><br />There’s also a lot of sex, which actually gave me something of a nostalgic glow. British horror writers of a 1970s/1980s vintage were always guaranteed to throw in a good few gratuitous sex scenes. I knew as an adolescent that I always more likely to get that kind of thing from a James Herbert than a Stephen King. Reading this not also made me yearn for my mis-spent youth, but it set me pondering: trying to figure out why it was that British horror was so adamant on combining heavy gore with detailed sex scenes. My best guess is that the British authors of this vintage were just over exposed to Hammer Horror movies and the buxom, blonde wenches who populated them. Certainly that seems to be the case of ‘Necroscope’, as the sex sequence with a blonde serving girl in an inn couldn’t have been written any more obviously with Ingrid Pitt in mind if Lumley had included a still from ‘The Vampire Lovers’.<br /><br />It’s not a perfect book by any means, the powers our protagonist and antagonist develop just become more and more ludicrous even within the framework of the book, while the confrontation between the two is oddly rushed. But if you were looking for a good British horror novel of the 80s – with all that sub genre’s interest in gore, sex, flawed heroes and drizzle – then ‘Necroscope’ would be a definite top recommendation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8685637872335055980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1051167557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1051167557" />
    <a title="Quentin Wallace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33274222-quentin-wallace"><img alt="Quentin Wallace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595984858p2/33274222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1051167557?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Quentin Wallace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Quentin Wallace" href="/user/show/33274222-quentin-wallace">Quentin Wallace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780812521375" href="/book/show/1063376.Necroscope">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1051167557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16580130973252161051">This one was..complicated. I finally got around to reading it after putting it off for a while, and I did enjoy it. However, it wasn't really what I expected and it did have its flaws.<br/><br/>First off, I think it's a little too lengthy. 100-200 pages could have been cut and it would have been a stronger, tighter story. The story is set during the Cold War, and we see Britain and Russia both utilizing ESP agents, as in agents with some type of mental power. Our two main characters are a necromancer, who</span>
  <span id="freeText16580130973252161051" style="display:none">This one was..complicated. I finally got around to reading it after putting it off for a while, and I did enjoy it. However, it wasn't really what I expected and it did have its flaws.<br /><br />First off, I think it's a little too lengthy. 100-200 pages could have been cut and it would have been a stronger, tighter story. The story is set during the Cold War, and we see Britain and Russia both utilizing ESP agents, as in agents with some type of mental power. Our two main characters are a necromancer, who can speak to the dead only by fondling their organs, and a necroscope, who can converse with the dead (and even control them as we find out later.) The necromancer is evil, but the necroscope is not. Then we end up with a vampire thrown in the mix. Lumley's vampires have most of the same powers and weaknesses as traditional vampires, but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ they are an actual, parasitic creature that exists in the human body. Once they are "infected", I mean.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Things get a little far out by the end, as it turns more into a superhero battling a supervillain rather than a necroscope battling a vampire. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I thought it was a bit much the necroscope could suddenly travel through time and space. Didn't seem to fit the story well to me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, I did enjoy it. It was plodding in some parts, nearing tedious. The character development was there although in some cases there was probably more than we needed. If you are looking for a traditional horror story, you'll probably be disappointed. If you enjoy horror, spy tales, and superhero stories, then you should like this one. Overall, I think this is one you just have to decide on for yourself. There are several books in the series, and I can't say whether I will read them all. I will however, read at least the next few to see where the story goes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16580130973252161051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer446944201444078768">Wow, okay, it took me a little longer than usual to get through this book. The amount of detail was a real slog at the beginning, but once you start getting into it, the story really takes off. There are still spots of deep deep deeeeeeep detail on par with something from Lord of Rings or something, which I guess is one way of describing the magnitude of this series, minus any metaphor or symbolism Tolkien was a master for, still, its kinda nice having the horror equivalent of his work. As for t</span>
  <span id="freeText446944201444078768" style="display:none">Wow, okay, it took me a little longer than usual to get through this book. The amount of detail was a real slog at the beginning, but once you start getting into it, the story really takes off. There are still spots of deep deep deeeeeeep detail on par with something from Lord of Rings or something, which I guess is one way of describing the magnitude of this series, minus any metaphor or symbolism Tolkien was a master for, still, its kinda nice having the horror equivalent of his work. As for the story, it was not what I originally believed it would be about, yeah, there are vampires, but not in a great abundance, but that's okay. The part of Harry's evolution was amazingly creative. Enjoyed this entry very much and am looking forward to starting book 2. </span>
