<div id="review_1411247533" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1411247533" />
    <a title="Ctgt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3787451-ctgt"><img alt="Ctgt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524569344p2/3787451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1411247533?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ctgt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ctgt" href="/user/show/3787451-ctgt">Ctgt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780812521375" href="/book/show/1063376.Necroscope">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3787451-ctgt?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1411247533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7771164648834791523">I really should have loved this book, set in the years after WII with the traditional Cold War adversaries and an added supernatural twist, competing divisions made up of agents with unusual abilities. But there were long passages of background information that I really struggled to wade through. This is a series of books so I guess you can consider this a set-up book but it just seemed like there could have been a better way to incorporate all the information without resorting to these extended</span>
  <span id="freeText7771164648834791523" style="display:none">I really should have loved this book, set in the years after WII with the traditional Cold War adversaries and an added supernatural twist, competing divisions made up of agents with unusual abilities. But there were long passages of background information that I really struggled to wade through. This is a series of books so I guess you can consider this a set-up book but it just seemed like there could have been a better way to incorporate all the information without resorting to these extended segments of info dumps. There are some great scenes, including a fantastically horrific autopsy that I won't soon forget and the powers some the agents possess offer great possibilities. So even with my unhappiness with parts of the book I will still check out the next book in the series. <br /><br />6/10</span>
  <a data-text-id="7771164648834791523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1407766959" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1407766959" />
    <a title="Perry Lake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29202636-perry-lake"><img alt="Perry Lake" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442970575p2/29202636.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1407766959?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Perry Lake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Perry Lake" href="/user/show/29202636-perry-lake">Perry Lake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780812521375" href="/book/show/1063376.Necroscope">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29202636-perry-lake?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29202636-perry-lake?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29202636-perry-lake?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1407766959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6516383079024102881">“NECROSCOPE”<br/>by Brian Lumley, 1986<br/><br/>I read half a dozen books by Brian Lumley in the early eighties, all on Lovecraftean themes. These included the Titus Crow and Borea adventures. I remember loving them.<br/><br/>Then Lumley turned to new material, his Necroscope series. This was more original than expanding on Lovecraft's themes, perhaps, but it wasn't what I was looking for at the time so I set them aside to collect dust. Recently, due to a Goodreads buddy read, I decided to give them a go.<br/><br/>The prolog of t</span>
  <span id="freeText6516383079024102881" style="display:none">“NECROSCOPE”<br />by Brian Lumley, 1986<br /><br />I read half a dozen books by Brian Lumley in the early eighties, all on Lovecraftean themes. These included the Titus Crow and Borea adventures. I remember loving them.<br /><br />Then Lumley turned to new material, his Necroscope series. This was more original than expanding on Lovecraft's themes, perhaps, but it wasn't what I was looking for at the time so I set them aside to collect dust. Recently, due to a Goodreads buddy read, I decided to give them a go.<br /><br />The prolog of this first book is seriously boring. Chapter 1 has its dramatic moments, but the book really only catches the reader's attention at Chapter 2 when we are introduced to young Harry Keogh, the hero of the series. Harry is a likeable teenager with the usual teenage problems of school, bullies, and girls. Oh, and he channels the dead.<br /><br />But Harry is not the only necroscope in town, er, the world. The Russians have their own channeler of the dead, the Romanian, Boris Dragosani. He works it a bit differently than our Harry, though, with his hands deep in the guts of corpses, tearing away their secrets. Then he sells these secrets to the KGB.<br /><br />Lumley certainly evokes a feeling for Romania, its sense of history, its place in the world, and under the shadow of the tottering colossus to the east. The book is set during the Cold War, when tensions between the two superpowers were high. Showing England and Romania, as satellites of the US and USSR, respectively, garners sympathy for both nations and their inhabitants. In the shadow of the two rival giants, these smaller nations were often manipulated into a fight that neither wanted.<br /><br />There's a drawn-out subplot about Boris's sexual frustration, but curiously, Boris is also likeable, in his way. After all, he didn't ask to be a necromancer. But eventually, he asks to become a Wamphyri, a vampire. Boris gains his powers from a Fifteenth Century Walachian nobleman who became a vampire and was imprisoned in a forgotten tomb. No, it's not Dracula, but it could have been.<br /><br />Things do start to get interesting after Harry and Boris meet and declare one another the enemy. Soon both of them use the dead to gain new skills; eventually, Harry learns to teleport and Boris learns to kill with only a glance.<br /><br />Curious to me, every single psychic in “Necroscope” is male. Having been involved with a parapsychological research group, I've found the majority of talented psychics to be female.<br /><br />As I said, years earlier I read Lumley's Titus Crow series and other books which are derived from themes and characters out of Lovecraft's mythos. But Lumley is not Lovecraft so his stories are more adventuresome than horrifying. He does the same thing here, but instead derives primarily from Bram Stoker. At times, he merges the two myth-cycles and for me that's very appealing.<br /><br />In both series, there are teams of psychics who are fighting the forces of evil. Or aiding them, as the case might be. Back when this was written, there were often stories in the press about the USSR's experiments with psychic phenomena. There was speculation that Russian spies would be able to use their minds to kill the President of the United States or divert atom bombs. This theme was used to humorous effect in “The Men Who Stared at Goats”.<br /><br />I found “Necroscope” more interesting as an idea than as an actual book, but there's still good material here. The action-packed ending heads right back into Lovecraftean territory, with Harry walking into angles that should not exist and popping up in a scene that I found hilarious in its audacity. More important though, there's some deep thought about the nature of Time, Space, and Eternity that seriously got me to thinking. It's worth a read for that alone.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6516383079024102881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2150900094" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2150900094" />
    <a title="S.E. Lindberg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5966698-s-e-lindberg"><img alt="S.E. Lindberg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433723737p2/5966698.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2150900094?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.E. Lindberg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.E. Lindberg" href="/user/show/5966698-s-e-lindberg">S.E. Lindberg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5966698-s-e-lindberg?shelf=reviewed-by-se">reviewed-by-se</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5966698-s-e-lindberg?shelf=weird-fiction">weird-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2150900094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7054287099575956490"><b>Weird ESPionage from the master of mashing up horror and adventure</b>:<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/20602.Brian_Lumley' title='Brian Lumley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Brian Lumley</a>'s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/66655.Necroscope__Necroscope___1_' title='Necroscope (Necroscope, #1) by Brian Lumley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Necroscope</a> is not heroic fiction, which I typically focus on. It is very entertaining and has connections to Weird Sword & Sorcery adventure which led me to read it:<br/><br/><u>1) Heroes of Dreams & Khash series</u>: I discovered Lumley’s writing via his Weird Sword & Sorcery. Vintage dark fantasy spawned in the early 1900’s from the work of pen-pals R.E. Howard and H.P. Lovecraft; though it seems rare to find quality Conan-Mythos</span>
  <span id="freeText7054287099575956490" style="display:none"><b>Weird ESPionage from the master of mashing up horror and adventure</b>:<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/20602.Brian_Lumley" title="Brian Lumley" rel="nofollow noopener">Brian Lumley</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/66655.Necroscope__Necroscope___1_" title="Necroscope (Necroscope, #1) by Brian Lumley" rel="nofollow noopener">Necroscope</a> is not heroic fiction, which I typically focus on. It is very entertaining and has connections to Weird Sword &amp; Sorcery adventure which led me to read it:<br /><br /><u>1) Heroes of Dreams &amp; Khash series</u>: I discovered Lumley’s writing via his Weird Sword &amp; Sorcery. Vintage dark fantasy spawned in the early 1900’s from the work of pen-pals R.E. Howard and H.P. Lovecraft; though it seems rare to find quality Conan-Mythos mash-ups. Brian Lumely has done so a few times. First, his <a href="http://www.selindberg.com/2016/12/lumleys-hero-of-dreams-review-by-se.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Hero of Dreams series</a> is an overt mashup of Lovecraft’s Dreamcycle and Leiber’s Fafred and Gray Mouser series. Lumley’s <a>Tarra Khash</a> series (a.k.a. Tales of Primal Land) was written in a similar vein (i.e. fun Sword &amp; Sorcery adventure in a Weird-Fiction, Cthulhu-esque world).<br /><br /><u>2) Blood Omen Legacy of Kain</u>: A huge fan of the Horror S&amp;S Game Series “Blood Omen: Legacy of Kain”, I was delighted to learn that Lumely’s writing influenced Denis Dyack’s vision of Nosgoth. Denis Dyack, creator of Silicon Knights, made the original Blood Omen: Legacy of Kain game (various incarnations from 1996 thru 2009). As a Kain fan I did not know the influence from Lumely until I saw an interview on Youtube (<a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q1pm0ix27tk&amp;t=17s" rel="nofollow noopener">The Quantum Tunnel 2016 called Blood Omen Legacy Of Kain Deep Dive 1</a>), in which Dyack reveals that the classic horror/action-rpg game was influenced by Lumey’s Necroscope series. Given the Visceral, Vampire, Lovecraftian, and Time Travel elements, this makes sense; however, the book has a contemporary setting versus the medieval one in the game.<br /><br />As a fan of Khash, Heroes of Dreams, and Legacy of Kain… I just had to check out Necroscope. So what is it really?<br /><br /><b>Necroscope is “ESPionage” fiction</b> (a word coined in this book), blending paranormal horror with spy adventure. It kicks off a series of 18 books (published 1986 to 2013). This first entry is entertaining and sets an expansive foundation for a wild ride. People with supernatural powers (predicting the future, speaking to the dead, etc.) are being enlisted into government agencies. <br /><br />The book is ostensibly about the battle between the United Kingdom vs. the Russian governments special forces, but the conflict is really about Harry Keogh (speaker to the dead) vs. Boris Dragosani (who approximates a vampire). Each is associated with a government, but each is motivated by personal goals which take center stage. The reader learns about supernatural powers as these two do. After they master their respective powers, they go to battle in a most bizarre way chock-full of undead things and over the top time travel.<br /><br />Expect lots of changing perspective and lots of story threads that will gel about half way through. Artwork is unexpectedly sprinkled throughout the book (even the Kindle version). The geometry puzzles and Moebius Strips shown relate the story and make for fun, relevant, diversions. This is very digestible horror for non-horror fans. A very fast read, recommended to just about everyone who likes dark adventure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7054287099575956490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_60636610" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60636610" />
    <a title="Ceri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2443968-ceri"><img alt="Ceri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492940562p2/2443968.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60636610?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ceri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ceri" href="/user/show/2443968-ceri">Ceri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765320186" href="/book/show/2225965.Necroscope">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60636610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6302021602423006825">Wow! It's nearly impossible to describe how I feel about this book. I was given it to read by my father - the pair of us share a mutual love of horror books and films. I'm always keen to read more vampire books but, good God, this is so much more than a vampire book.<br/><br/>When I started reading Necroscope, I couldn't help but notice that it was rather dated. From the summary on the back, and the rather slow and (unfortunately) clichéd beginning I had my doubts about what I was getting myself into it. </span>
  <span id="freeText6302021602423006825" style="display:none">Wow! It's nearly impossible to describe how I feel about this book. I was given it to read by my father - the pair of us share a mutual love of horror books and films. I'm always keen to read more vampire books but, good God, this is so much more than a vampire book.<br /><br />When I started reading Necroscope, I couldn't help but notice that it was rather dated. From the summary on the back, and the rather slow and (unfortunately) clichéd beginning I had my doubts about what I was getting myself into it. Slowly but surely, though, the story began to pick up. I understood what Lumley was doing. He doesn't want you to miss a thing. He wants you to know the ins and outs of every character in his story because, the moment the drama begins, that's when things get complicated. Let me give you a checklist of what to expect:<br /><br /> 1. E.S.P. - (We're talking telepathy, future predictions, mind control, evil eyes and, of course, talking to the dead)<br /> 2. Vampires (and their history)<br /> 3. Zombies<br /> 4. Time Travel (in a sense)<br /><br />It's a hell of a lot of detail to cram into one book but Lumley pulls if off perfectly. How he manages this is by introducing you to the characters when they are equally as clueless and naive about these things as you. Despire the fact that his two central heroes, Dragosani and Keogh, hold these formidable powers, their characters and backgrounds are well established and written out which makes you truly believe that these two men are really human and could really exist.<br /><br />The story itself is completely original - not what it would seem at first, so keep reading. We have Harry and Dragosani working for two seperate secret services - both of which run on E.S.P. talents. Then the vampires are thrown in. Then the talking (and walking) dead. And just before the story reaches it conclusion, elements of space and time travel are thrown in for extra measure.<br /><br />It's so difficult to completely describe how imaginative, exciting, and spine-tingling this story is. The words speak for themselves and, as a result, I can't give a full review on why I loved this. It's written wonderfully and is clearly something Lumley has taken the time to put together for his readers, inviting them to explore every speck of his imagination. This is the first book in a long series - a series I will definitely be pursuing in time to come because the story isn't over yet. I want to know what happens to those characters that are left behind. All I can say is, if you like a fun and fast-paced story, don't mind a bit of gore, and enjoy anything out of the ordinary, read it for yourself. You won't regret it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6302021602423006825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_649868938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/649868938" />
    <a title="Nick Borrelli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5427149-nick-borrelli"><img alt="Nick Borrelli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603556851p2/5427149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/649868938?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick Borrelli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick Borrelli" href="/user/show/5427149-nick-borrelli">Nick Borrelli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer649868938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6567562779201073751">This book was all the rage when it was first released, but boy it has not aged well. The three star rating is basically due to the fact that it feels really dated because of the cold war aspects to the story. Harry Keough is a Necroscope, which means for all intents and purposes, he can communicate with the undead. Harry works for a secret branch of the U.S. government that is trying to infiltrate and discover what they suspect is going on with their Russian counter-parts in the KGB. It seem the</span>
  <span id="freeText6567562779201073751" style="display:none">This book was all the rage when it was first released, but boy it has not aged well. The three star rating is basically due to the fact that it feels really dated because of the cold war aspects to the story. Harry Keough is a Necroscope, which means for all intents and purposes, he can communicate with the undead. Harry works for a secret branch of the U.S. government that is trying to infiltrate and discover what they suspect is going on with their Russian counter-parts in the KGB. It seem they also have a secret branch that is breeding vampires in an attempt to gain the upper hand against the Americans. The story is really good if say you were reading it in 1989. The problem is that the bulk of the story relies on the cold war angle, which anyone born after the year 1992 isn't going to connect with. If you can put aside the dated feel, then by all means give it a whirl. I just couldn't do it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6567562779201073751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZotKtx7Npd7+ZjVlGTPNFwzuQ6CkrnJyzQEeCL0DBKIR2uPeMl30Fhr7Kbwfjjo6II8zZ8P3S2LSclM6gcQ8Jw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fjEjzRi/rGGbVChgXS0gODDZHPhvUYIizMw1kwMPZhIJYIqkNC/9qX/JNLlbkNcVHLhsPwgIuzLTv3ihP8helw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15554520025425480515">Brian Lumley was born near Newcastle. In 22 years as a Military Policeman he served in many of the Cold War hotspots, including Berlin, as well as Cyprus in partition days. He reached the rank of Sergeant-Major before retiring to Devon to write full-time, and his work was first published in 1970. The vampire series, 'Necroscope', has been translated into ten languages and sold over a million copie</span>
  <span id="freeText15554520025425480515" style="display:none">Brian Lumley was born near Newcastle. In 22 years as a Military Policeman he served in many of the Cold War hotspots, including Berlin, as well as Cyprus in partition days. He reached the rank of Sergeant-Major before retiring to Devon to write full-time, and his work was first published in 1970. The vampire series, 'Necroscope', has been translated into ten languages and sold over a million copies worldwide.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /></span>
